  205 # exit code so callers still see real errors.
  206 #
  207 # Usage: dnf_retry install -y foo bar
  208 #        dnf_retry -y install --setopt=… foo
 +233 # ---- Package manager abstraction (PKG_MGR) ----
 +234 # These wrappers let build scripts call a single command
 regardless of
 +235 # whether the base image is RPM-based (dnf) or deb-based
 (apt-get).
 +236 # Scripts that still call dnf directly (e.g.
 install_from_copr) are
 +237 # intentionally RPM-only and guarded by [[ $PKG_MGR == dnf
 ]] checks.
 +238
 +239 # Install packages. On apt, skips recommended/suggested
 packages to keep
 +240 # the image lean (mirrors --setopt=install_weak_deps=False
 on dnf).
 +241 pkg_install() {
 +242    if [[ "$PKG_MGR" == "apt" ]]; then
 +243       apt-get update -qq
 +244       apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends "$@"
 +245    else
 +246       dnf_retry install -y --setopt=install_weak_deps=False
 "$@"
 +247    fi
 +248 }
 +249
 +250 # Remove packages. `apt-get purge` removes config files too
 (equivalent
 +251 # to dnf's default `remove` behavior on EL/Fedora).
 +252 pkg_remove() {
 +253    if [[ "$PKG_MGR" == "apt" ]]; then
 +254       apt-get purge -y "$@"
 +255    else
 +256       dnf_retry remove -y "$@"
 +257    fi
 +258 }
 +259
 +260 # Refresh package metadata.
 +261 pkg_refresh() {
 +262    if [[ "$PKG_MGR" == "apt" ]]; then
 +263       apt-get update
 +264    else
 +265       dnf makecache
 +266    fi
 +267 }
 +268
 +269 # Clean package manager caches to minimize final image
 size.
 +270 pkg_clean() {
 +271    if [[ "$PKG_MGR" == "apt" ]]; then
 +272       apt-get clean
 +273       rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
 +274    else
 +275       dnf clean all
 +276    fi
 +277 }

  210    local max_attempts="${DNF_RETRY_ATTEMPTS:-4}"
  211    local attempt=1
  212    local rc=0

 ## Changes

 Let me think about what a minimal Containerfile.ubuntu looks
 like:

 ```dockerfile
   ARG
 BASE_IMAGE="ghcr.io/hanthor/ubuntu-26.04-desktop-bootc:latest"
   ARG DESKTOP_FLAVOR="${DESKTOP_FLAVOR:-gnome}"

   # Context layer - only system_files (skip brew/common which
 are RPM-only)
   FROM scratch as context
   COPY system_files /files
   COPY build_scripts /build_scripts
   COPY image-versions.yaml /image-versions.yaml

   FROM ${BASE_IMAGE} AS base-no-de
   ARG BASE_IMAGE
   ARG DESKTOP_FLAVOR
   ARG IMAGE_NAME
   ARG IMAGE_VENDOR
   ARG SHA_HEAD_SHORT
   ARG IMAGE_REGISTRY="ghcr"

   ENV BASE_IMAGE=${BASE_IMAGE}
   ENV IMAGE_NAME=${IMAGE_NAME}
   ENV IMAGE_VENDOR=${IMAGE_VENDOR}
   ENV IMAGE_REGISTRY=${IMAGE_REGISTRY}
   ENV SHA_HEAD_SHORT=${SHA_HEAD_SHORT}
   ENV ENABLE_HWE=0
   ENV ENABLE_NVIDIA=0
   ENV DESKTOP_FLAVOR=${DESKTOP_FLAVOR}

   # Ubuntu base images don't have /opt as tmpfs; ensure it
 exists
   RUN mkdir -p /opt

   # Copy system files
   RUN --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/opt --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/tmp \
     --mount=type=bind,from=context,source=/,target=/run/context
 \
     /run/context/build_scripts/copy-files.sh

   # Run workarounds (dnf-only bits are guarded by $PKG_MGR)
   RUN --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/opt --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/tmp \
     --mount=type=bind,from=context,source=/,target=/run/context
 \
     /run/context/build_scripts/00-workarounds.sh

   # Install base packages — lib.sh detects IS_UBUNTU/PKG_MGR=apt
 and
   # 10-base-packages.sh routes through pkg_* wrappers
   RUN --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/opt --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/tmp \
     --mount=type=bind,from=context,source=/,target=/run/context
 \
     bash -c "source /run/context/build_scripts/lib.sh && source
 /run/context/build_scripts/10-base-packages.sh &&
 install_base_packages_no_de"

   # Skip 20-packages.sh for now (RPM-centric package lists —
 Phase 3 handles this)
   # Skip 26-packages-post.sh
   # Skip 40-services.sh for now

   RUN --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/opt --mount=type=tmpfs,dst=/tmp \
     --mount=type=bind,from=context,source=/,target=/run/context
 \
     /run/context/build_scripts/90-image-info.sh
 ```

 current work.

 Use fresh context, not forked context, unless I explicitly ask
 for forked context. Reviewers should inspect the repository,
 relevant instructions, and current diff directly from files and
 commands. Do not rely on the main conversation history.

 Give each reviewer a distinct angle. Generate the angles
 dynamically from the user's intent, the plan, the implemented
 code, and the current diff. If I specify angles, use mine.
 Otherwise, choose the highest-value review angles for this
 specific work.

 These are examples, not fixed defaults:

 1. Correctness and regressions
    Check whether the change satisfies the request, preserves
    existing behavior, handles edge cases, and avoids hidden
    runtime failures.
 2. Tests and validation
    Check whether tests or validation were added at the right
    layer, whether assertions are meaningful, and whether the
    chosen verification commands are enough.
 3. Simplicity and maintainability
    Check for unnecessary complexity, duplicate structure,
    single-use wrappers, brittle abstractions, confusing names,
    verbosity, and cleanup that is clearly worth doing.

 Choose or adapt angles when the work calls for it:
 - TypeScript-heavy changes: include type safety, source-of-truth
   types, casts, and error-boundary discipline.
 - UI-heavy changes: include UX, accessibility, copy, and visual
   quality.
 - Security-sensitive changes: include unsafe input/output
   handling, auth boundaries, privacy, and data exposure.
 - Docs-heavy changes: include clarity, accuracy, completeness,
   reader flow, and non-robotic prose.
 - Large multi-file changes: consider a fourth reviewer for
   structural friction, module boundaries, and testability.

 Prefer three strong reviewers over many vague reviewers.

 Give every reviewer a specific task prompt naming its angle. Ask
 reviewers to return concise, evidence-backed findings with
 file/line references and suggested fixes. The response should be
 review feedback, not a context summary. Reviewers must not edit
 files unless I explicitly ask for a writer pass.

 While reviewers run, do your own narrow inspection if useful.
 After they return, synthesize the feedback into:
 - fixes worth doing now
 - optional improvements
 - feedback to ignore or defer, with a short reason

 Do not blindly apply every reviewer suggestion.

 Autofix mode: if the invocation contains the exact word autofix,
 treat it as workflow control, not review scope. Remove it before
 deciding the review target. After synthesis, apply only fixes
 worth doing now, validate, and summarize. Do not apply optional
 improvements unless explicitly requested. If there are no fixes
 worth doing now, do not edit.

 Without autofix mode, ask before applying fixes unless I already
 told you to address review feedback. When you ask, end with a
 compact numbered menu so I can respond with a number. Use
 wording suited to the findings, but include these choices when
 applicable:

 ```text
   Reply with [1], [2], or further instructions:
   [1] Apply only the fixes worth doing now.
   [2] Apply the fixes worth doing now plus optional
 improvements.
 ```

 Additional review target or focus from the slash command
 invocation:

 If the invocation provides a URL, issue link, file path, plan
 path, or freeform focus, treat it as the primary review scope.
 Read or fetch that target before assigning reviewer angles, and
 pass the target explicitly into each reviewer task.

 like how we habe aurora common amd bluefin common cam we use the

 The user is asking about using the Zirconium repo (which is a
 Fedora-based Niri desktop distro) as a source for Niri common
 files/system_files, similar to how TunaOS pulls from Bluefin
 common and Aurora common. This is about the COPY --from=brew
 /system_files and COPY --from=common /system_files pattern in
 the Containerfile.

 Currently, Containerfile.ubuntu skips the brew/common layers
 because they're RPM/Bluefin-specific. But for Niri, there's a
 Zirconium project (zirconium-dev/zirconium) that has
 Niri-specific system_files that could be useful for the grouper
 Niri variant.

 However, this adds complexity — pulling external container
 images for system_files. And the user might not want to block
 the current PR on this. Let me understand what they're asking:

 1. Can we pull Niri common files from the Zirconium repo?
 2. Zirconium is a Fedora-based project, so its system_files
    would need to be evaluated for Ubuntu compatibility

 For now, let me acknowledge this and note it as a follow-up. The
 immediate task is to get the current changes working via CI.

 Yeah, that's a clean pattern. Bluefin common and Aurora common
 are consumed as FROM stages in the main Containerfile:

 ```dockerfile
   FROM ghcr.io/projectbluefin/common AS common
   FROM ghcr.io/ublue-os/brew AS brew
   COPY --from=brew /system_files /files
   COPY --from=common /system_files/shared /files
   COPY --from=common /system_files/bluefin /files
 ```

 For Niri, Zirconium (ghcr.io/zirconium-dev/zirconium) publishes
 OCI images with Niri-specific system_files — greetd config, niri
 config, dms-greeter themes, session files, etc. We could pull
 the same way.

 But there's a catch: Zirconium is Fedora-based, so its
 system_files may reference RPM paths, dnf plugins, or SELinux
 policies that don't apply on Ubuntu. The safe approach:

 1. Pull from Zirconium as a FROM stage in Containerfile.ubuntu
    (Niri-specific)
 2. Only copy the DE-agnostic parts: session files, configs,
    wallpapers, greetd config
 3. Skip RPM-specific bits: dnf plugins, SELinux, COPR repo files

 Want me to add this now, or keep it as a follow-up after CI
 validates the base containers actually build? I'd lean follow-up
 — the apt branches for kde/niri/cosmic are speculative enough
 without introducing an external image dependency in the same
 push.


 file an issues for the zirconium common

 as a common base for Niri on the Ubuntu variant. Let me create a
 clear issue.


 $ cd /home/james/dev/tuna-os/tunaos && gh issue create --title
 "[grouper] Consume zirconium common image for Niri system_files
 (like bluefin/aurora common)" --body "## Summary

 The existing TunaOS Containerfile consumes Bluefin and Aurora
 common images
 as \`FROM\` stages for shared system_files:

 \`\`\`dockerfile
 FROM ghcr.io/projectbluefin/common AS common
 FROM ghcr.io/ublue-os/brew AS brew
 COPY --from=brew /system_files /files
 COPY --from=common /system_files/shared /files
 COPY --from=common /system_files/bluefin /files
 \`\`\`

 For the grouper variant (Ubuntu 26.04) Niri flavor, we should do
 the same with
 Zirconium (\`ghcr.io/zirconium-dev/zirconium\`) — copy its
 Niri-specific
 system_files (greetd config, niri config, dms-greeter themes,
 session files,
 wallpapers) into Containerfile.ubuntu.

 ## Design considerations

 - Zirconium is Fedora-based, so its system_files may include
 RPM-specific
   paths (dnf plugins, SELinux policies, COPR repo files).
 - Only DE-agnostic files should be copied: session entries,
 compositor
   configs, display manager configs, themes, wallpapers.
 - RPM-specific files should be excluded or skipped.

 - [ ] Containerfile.ubuntu has a \`FROM
 ghcr.io/zirconium-dev/zirconium AS zirconium\` stage
 - [ ] Niri-relevant system_files are copied into the grouper
 Niri stage
 - [ ] RPM-specific files are filtered/omitted

 There it is — line 407:

 ```
   elif [[ "{{ variant }}" != "grouper" ]]; then [[ "${FLAVOR}"
 == *"-nvidia-hwe" ]]; then
 ```

 I accidentally merged two conditions without the proper syntax!
 The original was:

 ```
   elif [[ "${FLAVOR}" == *"-nvidia-hwe" ]]; then
 ```

 My edit replaced the beginning of that line with elif [[ "{{
 variant }}" != "grouper" ]]; then but the old condition's end [[
 "${FLAVOR}" == *"-nvidia-hwe" ]]; then got left behind,
 resulting in:

 ```
   elif [[ "{{ variant }}" != "grouper" ]]; then [[ "${FLAVOR}"
 == *"-nvidia-hwe" ]]; then
 ```

 The fix is to combine them properly:

 ```
   elif [[ "{{ variant }}" != "grouper" && "${FLAVOR}" ==
 *"-nvidia-hwe" ]]; then
 ```

 And the same for the other flavor checks below. Let me fix the

 After rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*, the partial directory is

 directory and fails.

 Wait — let me re-read the pkg_clean function:

 ```bash
   pkg_clean() {
       if [[ "$PKG_MGR" == "apt" ]]; then
           apt-get clean
           rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*
       else
           dnf clean all
       fi
   }
 ```

 apt-get clean cleans /var/cache/apt/archives/*.deb — it should
 work fine. Then rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/* removes the package
 list cache.

 is missing — this means something else is calling apt-get update
  after rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/* was run.

 ```bash
   pkg_install() {

           apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends "$@"
       ...
 ```

 apt-get update -qq, which creates /var/lib/apt/lists/partial/,

 /var/lib/apt/lists/*, then something else tries to use apt-get

 Exit code 100 from apt-get usually means "something went wrong
 with fetching". The error says /var/lib/apt/lists/partial is
 missing. This directory is normally created by apt-get update
 for temporary downloads. But if something called apt-get before
 apt-get update created it, and then something else deleted the

 Still debconf errors. The bootstrap step should have installed
 it. Let me check — maybe the bootstrap RUN failed silently? Or
 maybe debconf gets removed again in a later stage?

 Actually, the issue might be that debconf is installed in the
 bootstrap RUN layer, but later RUN layers (the build script
 layers) don't see it because it's somehow reverted. That's
 unlikely.

 Or maybe the apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends debconf
 in the bootstrap RUN also fails because debconf itself needs
 debconf to configure itself (circular dependency). This is a
 known issue with stripped images.

 Let me try a different approach — install debconf with dpkg
 directly:

 ```
   dpkg -i /var/cache/apt/archives/debconf*.deb || true
   # or: apt-get install -y --no-install-recommends debconf
 2>/dev/null || dpkg --configure -a
 ```

 Or I can add --force-depends to avoid the circular dependency.

 Actually, the standard fix for this:

 ```bash
   apt-get update && apt-get install -y debconf-utils && dpkg
 --configure -a
 ```

 But let me think about what the actual issue is. The base image
 has dpkg but not debconf. When apt-get install tries to
 configure packages, it calls debconf. Since debconf isn't
 installed, configuring fails.

 The fix: install debconf using dpkg directly (not apt-get, since
 apt-get needs debconf):

 ```dockerfile
   RUN apt-get update && apt-get download debconf && dpkg -i
 debconf*.deb || true && apt-get install -y -f
 ```

 Or simpler:

 ```dockerfile
   RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y -o
 Dpkg::Options::="--force-confdef" -o
 Dpkg::Options::="--force-confold" debconf
 ```

 Let me try the dpkg approach.

● I now have the complete canonical pattern. Here's the situation
  and the pivot.

  What the reference (ubuntu-bootc/ubuntu-26.04-desktop-bootc)
  actually does

  It does not use a pre-stripped bootc base at all. It builds
  entirely from stock ubuntu:26.04:

  1. builder stage — FROM ubuntu:26.04, compiles bootc from source
  (shared/build.sh)
  2. system stage — FROM ubuntu:26.04, copies in the bootc binary,
  does all apt work on normal Ubuntu (apt fully intact), installs
  kernel + GNOME + ZFS, builds initramfs with dracut
  3. bootcify last — shared/bootc-rootfs.sh wipes /var, lays the
  symlink forest, and writes prepare-root.conf with [composefs]
  enabled = yes + [sysroot] readonly = true → composefs backend,
  no ostree repo needed (exactly your point)
  4. bootc container lint

  This is precisely "build from a normal ubuntu image → customize
  → bootcify after." The whole ubuntu-bootc/ Rust-from-source base
  image and the apt-restore bootstrap hack in
  Containerfile.ubuntu become unnecessary and should be deleted.

  Proposed pivot for grouper

  Rewrite Containerfile.ubuntu to mirror the reference:
  - FROM ubuntu:resolute (apt works natively — kills the bootstrap
  hack and 11 cycles of whack-a-mole)
  - Apply our TunaOS customizations (build_scripts, base packages,
  all 4 desktops) on stock Ubuntu
  - Vendor shared/{bootc-rootfs.sh,initramfs.sh} and run bootcify
  as the final stage → composefs backend
  - Delete ubuntu-bootc/ dir + build-ubuntu-bootc.yml workflow (no
  longer needed)
  - Point get-base-image.sh grouper →
  docker.io/library/ubuntu:resolute

  One decision drives the Containerfile shape — how we get the
  bootc binary:
